<p><b>Jordan Brian Henderson</b> (born 17 June 1990) is an English professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a>.
</p><p>Henderson joined the <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" title="Sunderland A.F.C. Reserves and Academy">Sunderland Academy</a> at the age of eight, making his first-team debut a decade later in November 2008. He spent six months on <a href="/wiki/Loan_(sports)" title="Loan (sports)">loan</a> at <a href="/wiki/Coventry_City_F.C." title="Coventry City F.C.">Coventry City</a> in 2009, before returning to Sunderland. In 2011, Henderson signed for Liverpool, winning his first trophy with the club, the <a href="/wiki/2012_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2012 Football League Cup Final">League Cup</a>, one year later. Appointed Liverpool <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> in 2015, Henderson won the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">UEFA Champions League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2019 UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2019 FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> in 2019, and in 2020 led his team to the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Premier_League" title="2019–20 Premier League">Premier League title</a>, the club's first league title in 30 years. For his performances in the title winning season, Henderson was named <a href="/wiki/FWA_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="FWA Footballer of the Year">FWA Footballer of the Year</a>.
</p><p>An England international, Henderson has made over 50 appearances for his country since his debut in 2010. He has appeared at four international tournaments with England, the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">2012</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">2016</a> <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">UEFA European Championships</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014</a> and <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a>. He has won the <a href="/wiki/The_FA_England_Awards#Senior_Men&#39;s_Player_of_the_Year" title="The FA England Awards">England Player of the Year</a> award twice, both at U-21 and senior level, making him the first English player to do so.
</p>

</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sunderland">Sunderland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Sunderland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Henderson was born in <a href="/wiki/Sunderland" title="Sunderland">Sunderland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear" title="Tyne and Wear">Tyne and Wear</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and joined the youth system of his hometown club <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> aged eight.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He signed a professional contract with the club on 1 July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He made his league debut on 1 November 2008 in a 5–0 away defeat to <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> coming on as a half-time <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He then made his first Sunderland start and home debut against <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Football_League_Cup" title="2008–09 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Coventry_City_.28loan.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Coventry_City_(loan)">Coventry City (loan)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Coventry City (loan)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In January 2009, Henderson joined <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> club <a href="/wiki/Coventry_City_F.C." title="Coventry City F.C.">Coventry City</a> on a one-month <a href="/wiki/Loan_(sports)" title="Loan (sports)">loan</a> deal.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He made his Coventry debut in a 2–1 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Henderson's loan to Coventry was extended until the end of the season,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and he scored the first senior goal of his career on 28 February 2009 against <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> After picking up an injury, a fracture to the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_metatarsal_bone" title="Fifth metatarsal bone">fifth metatarsal bone</a> in his foot, he returned to Sunderland in April 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Sunderland">Return to Sunderland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Return to Sunderland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Henderson.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Jordan_Henderson.jpg/170px-Jordan_Henderson.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Jordan_Henderson.jpg/255px-Jordan_Henderson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Jordan_Henderson.jpg/340px-Jordan_Henderson.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1219" data-file-height="2001" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Henderson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henderson playing for <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Sunderland_A.F.C._season" title="2009–10 Sunderland A.F.C. season">2009–10 season</a>, Henderson broke into the Sunderland first team and made 33 <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Premier_League" title="2009–10 Premier League">Premier League</a> appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-sb0910_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sb0910-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first senior goal for the club against <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> in the League Cup third round.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He then went on to score his first Premier League goal against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> on 19 December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson spent the majority of the season on the right side of midfield but played centrally in the absence of <a href="/wiki/Lee_Cattermole" title="Lee Cattermole">Lee Cattermole</a>; his versatility and consistency earning him a new five-year contract on 23 April 2010, keeping him with the club until 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He also went on to win the Sunderland Young Player of the Year award for the 2009–10 season.<sup id="cite_ref-poy10_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poy10-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson was a major part of the team during the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Sunderland_A.F.C._season" title="2010–11 Sunderland A.F.C. season">2010–11 season</a> making 39 appearances and scoring 3 goals,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> including his first league double, on 23 April at home to <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> On 13 January 2011, Henderson was listed on the official FIFA website as one of 13 young players to watch in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He was named Sunderland's Young Player of the Year for the second season running.<sup id="cite_ref-poy11_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poy11-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liverpool">Liverpool</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Liverpool">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="2011.E2.80.932015:_Breaking_into_the_first_team"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–2015:_Breaking_into_the_first_team">2011–2015: Breaking into the first team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2011–2015: Breaking into the first team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Henderson_Liverpool_vs_Bolton_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jordan_Henderson_Liverpool_vs_Bolton_2011.jpg/170px-Jordan_Henderson_Liverpool_vs_Bolton_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jordan_Henderson_Liverpool_vs_Bolton_2011.jpg/255px-Jordan_Henderson_Liverpool_vs_Bolton_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Jordan_Henderson_Liverpool_vs_Bolton_2011.jpg/340px-Jordan_Henderson_Liverpool_vs_Bolton_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="465" data-file-height="818" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Henderson_Liverpool_vs_Bolton_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henderson playing for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>On 9 June 2011, Henderson was transferred to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> for an undisclosed fee thought to be between £16 and £20&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Liverpool_complete_Jordan_Henderson_deal_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liverpool_complete_Jordan_Henderson_deal-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut in Liverpool's first match of the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Premier_League" title="2011–12 Premier League">2011–12 Premier League</a>, a 1–1 draw against his former club Sunderland where he was given a mixed reception by Sunderland fans.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 27 August 2011, Henderson scored his first goal for Liverpool in a Premier League fixture at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> against <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> On 26 February 2012, Henderson started on the right of midfield in Liverpool's <a href="/wiki/2012_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2012 Football League Cup Final">2012 League Cup Final</a> victory over <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> before being substituted in the 58th minute.<sup id="cite_ref-2012LC_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012LC-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On 5 May, he played the full 90 minutes as Liverpool were beaten 2–1 by Chelsea in the <a href="/wiki/2012_FA_Cup_Final" title="2012 FA Cup Final">2012 FA Cup Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2012FAC_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012FAC-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Henderson ended the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2011–12 Liverpool F.C. season">2011–12 season</a> with two goals from 44 appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-sb1112_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sb1112-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2012, Henderson was told he could be signed by <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> by new manager <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Rodgers" title="Brendan Rodgers">Brendan Rodgers</a>, but this was rejected by the player.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He went on to score his first <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C._in_European_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool F.C. in European football">European</a> goal for Liverpool on 6 December 2012, with the winner against <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> as the <i>Reds</i> qualified for the last 32.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson established himself as a regular member of the Liverpool team in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2013–14 Liverpool F.C. season">2013–14 season</a>, playing in 35 <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">Premier League</a> matches and scoring 5 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On 29 September 2013, he made his 100th appearance for the club as Liverpool won 1–3 at Sunderland.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 13 April 2014 he received his first career <a href="/wiki/Ejection_(sports)" title="Ejection (sports)">red card</a> for a dangerous sliding tackle on <a href="/wiki/Samir_Nasri" title="Samir Nasri">Samir Nasri</a> in a 3–2 win over Manchester City, resulting in a three match ban which meant he would miss three of Liverpool's last four matches;<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> without Henderson, Liverpool lost 0–2 in a home game against Chelsea and drew 3–3 with <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>, losing a 3–0 lead in just 15 minutes before the final whistle.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Failure to win 3 points in each of those games meant Liverpool had already been succeeded by Manchester City in the first place by the time of Henderson's return from suspension. On 11 May 2014, the final match day of the competition, he started in Liverpool's 2–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> only to finish second as Manchester City claimed the league title in their concurrent game.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson started the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Liverpool F.C. season">2014–15 season</a> in a good form, providing two assists in Liverpool's first three league matches,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and was named as the club's <a href="/wiki/Vice-captain_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice-captain (association football)">vice-captain</a> following the departure of <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Agger" title="Daniel Agger">Daniel Agger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On 29 November, Henderson started as <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> for the first time for Liverpool in the Premier League against <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> as <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a> was an unused substitute.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On 2 December, Henderson marked his 150th appearance for the club by scoring the third goal in a 3–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> to confirm the win.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Henderson started many Liverpool matches as captain as Gerrard was out injured or being rested on the bench.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 23 April, Henderson signed a five-year contract extension at Liverpool worth £100,000 a week.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.93present:_Club_captain_and_European_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–present:_Club_captain_and_European_success">2015–present: Club captain and European success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2015–present: Club captain and European success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following the departure of Gerrard in June 2015, Henderson was made captain of Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> After aggravating a heel injury Henderson underwent surgery,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> but broke a bone in his right foot before he could rejoin the starting line-up.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> It was reported that Henderson's heel problems stemmed from the incurable condition <a href="/wiki/Plantar_fasciitis" title="Plantar fasciitis">plantar fasciitis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
The injury meant that he missed the arrival of manager <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klopp" title="Jürgen Klopp">Jürgen Klopp</a> after Rodgers was sacked.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He returned to first-team football on 29 November 2015 against <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> He scored on his first start since his injury, in a 2–2 home draw with <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> on 13 December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Knee" title="Knee">knee</a> injury sustained during Liverpool's Europa League first leg clash with <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> ruled him out until the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Henderson ended the 2015–16 season with 26 appearances and 2 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson started the 2016–17 season with regular appearances in the starting eleven and on 16 September scored a spectacular 25-yard strike in a 2–1 win over Chelsea at <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The strike earned him the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Goal_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Goal of the Month">Premier League Goal of the Month</a> award for the month of September.<sup id="cite_ref-goalofmonth_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goalofmonth-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Henderson ended the season with 27 appearances, scoring 1 goal.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson spent the 2017–18 season as a first-team regular, on 23 September 2017 he scored his only goal of the season, a winner against <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> in a 3–2 win.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On 15 August 2017 Henderson captained Liverpool for the first time in the Champions League against German side <a href="/wiki/TSG_1899_Hoffenheim" title="TSG 1899 Hoffenheim">Hoffenheim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He would go on to captain Liverpool all the way to the <a href="/wiki/2018_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2018 UEFA Champions League Final">final</a>, ending up on the losing side after Liverpool were beaten 3–1 by <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Henderson ended the 2017–18 season with 41 appearances in all competitions, scoring 1 goal.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson signed a new five-year deal at Liverpool in 2018 after leading the club to its first UEFA Champions League final in over a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> After signing the contract, Henderson emphasised his intentions to remain at Liverpool for as long as possible and ideally the remainder of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On 24 November, Henderson was sent off after receiving a second yellow card in a 3–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>, meaning he would miss the <a href="/wiki/Merseyside_derby" title="Merseyside derby">Merseyside derby</a> on 2 December.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 May 2019, Henderson played through pain after suffering a first half knee injury to captain Liverpool to qualification for their second <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> final in as many seasons with a 4–3 aggregate semi-final victory over <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>, a 4–0 victory on the night. Liverpool began the match with a 3–0 deficit to overcome and key players missing, and the comeback is considered to be one of the best in the history of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 June 2019, Henderson captained Liverpool in a 2–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">2019 UEFA Champions League Final</a> in Madrid, becoming the fifth Liverpool captain to lift the Champions League trophy,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> the club's sixth overall.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Liverpool then followed this up by winning the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2019 UEFA Super Cup">2019 UEFA Super Cup</a>, beating Chelsea on penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-2019UEFASuperCup_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019UEFASuperCup-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2019, Henderson led Liverpool to their first <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> title, making them the only English club to win the treble of continental trophies.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> After this third trophy in a year, ex-Liverpool player <a href="/wiki/John_Aldridge" title="John Aldridge">John Aldridge</a> voiced his belief that Henderson should now be regarded as a Liverpool great.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Liverpool finished the 2018–19 season with one of the highest points totals in English top-flight history, but finished in 2nd place one point behind champions Manchester City.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Liverpool's good form continued into the following season, and after a break caused by the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, Henderson led Liverpool to their first league title in 30 years on 25 June 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Often credited for heroic and passionate performances throughout the league-winning season, Henderson was named the <a href="/wiki/FWA_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="FWA Footballer of the Year">FWA Footballer of the Year</a> for 2020 along with being named a finalist for the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Player_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="PFA Player of the Year">PFA Player of the Year</a>. Having featured in 40 games during the 2019–20 season, Henderson entered the list of top 40 all-time Liverpool appearance makers at the end of the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henderson_Captaining_ENG-U-21.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Henderson_Captaining_ENG-U-21.jpg/170px-Henderson_Captaining_ENG-U-21.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Henderson_Captaining_ENG-U-21.jpg/255px-Henderson_Captaining_ENG-U-21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Henderson_Captaining_ENG-U-21.jpg/340px-Henderson_Captaining_ENG-U-21.jpg 2x" data-file-width="928" data-file-height="1514" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henderson_Captaining_ENG-U-21.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henderson playing for <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">England U21s</a> in 2012</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth">Youth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Youth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Henderson made his debut for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-19_football_team" title="England national under-19 football team">under-19s</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_national_under-19_football_team" title="Czech Republic national under-19 football team">Czech Republic</a> in 2009, before breaking into <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Pearce" title="Stuart Pearce">Stuart Pearce</a>'s <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">under-21</a> squad. He scored his first goal in an England shirt in the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship_qualification" title="2011 UEFA European Under-21 Championship qualification">European U21 Championship play-offs</a> against <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_under-21_football_team" title="Romania national under-21 football team">Romania</a>, hitting a volley from outside the box to give England the lead.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson was selected in the England U21 squad for the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship" title="2011 UEFA European Under-21 Championship">2011 European Championships</a>. However, England were knocked out in the group stage.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> He captained the England U21 team in a 6–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_national_under-21_football_team" title="Azerbaijan national under-21 football team">Azerbaijan U21</a> on 1 September 2011, scoring one goal in the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship_qualification" title="2013 UEFA European Under-21 Championship qualification">Euro 2013 qualifier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> He then scored his fourth under-21 goal in a 2–1 win away at <a href="/wiki/Norway_national_under-21_football_team" title="Norway national under-21 football team">Norway</a>, maintaining England's 100% record in Euro 2013 qualification.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> On 3 February 2013, Henderson was named the <a href="/wiki/England_Player_of_the_Year#England_Men&#39;s_U21_Player_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="England Player of the Year">England U21 Player of the Year</a> in the inaugural year of the award.<sup id="cite_ref-u21p_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-u21p-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> He captained the under-21 team at the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship" title="2013 UEFA European Under-21 Championship">2013 UEFA European Under-21 Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior">Senior</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Senior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Henderson_2018-06-28_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Jordan_Henderson_2018-06-28_1.jpg/170px-Jordan_Henderson_2018-06-28_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Jordan_Henderson_2018-06-28_1.jpg/255px-Jordan_Henderson_2018-06-28_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Jordan_Henderson_2018-06-28_1.jpg/340px-Jordan_Henderson_2018-06-28_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="369" data-file-height="528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Henderson_2018-06-28_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henderson with <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>On 11 November 2010, Henderson was omitted from England's U21 squad for their friendly with <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_under-21_football_team" title="Germany national under-21 football team">Germany</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> instead receiving his first call up to the senior England squad on 17 November 2010 for their friendly against <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut in the match, playing from the start in central midfield alongside Steven Gerrard.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Initially named as a standby player,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Henderson was called up to the England <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a> squad to replace the injured <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> He featured in England's first match of the tournament against France, coming on as a substitute in the 78th minute for <a href="/wiki/Scott_Parker" title="Scott Parker">Scott Parker</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and again featured as a substitute, coming on during extra-time, in England's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_knockout_stage" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Euro 2012 knockout stage">quarter-final</a> <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> defeat to <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson was selected in Roy Hodgson's 23-man squad to travel to Brazil for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> He started in England's opening two World Cup group matches, 2–1 defeats  to Italy in <a href="/wiki/Manaus" title="Manaus">Manaus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a> in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson was also selected in the England <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a> squad by Roy Hodgson.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> He only played one match, playing the full 90 minutes in the final group match against <a href="/wiki/Slovakia_national_football_team" title="Slovakia national football team">Slovakia</a> which ended 0–0 as England finished second in their group.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was named in the 23-man <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a> squad for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In England's Round of 16 match against <a href="/wiki/Colombia_national_football_team" title="Colombia national football team">Colombia</a>, Henderson was the only Three Lions player to miss a spot-kick as the match went to penalties. England still won though, 4–3, and made it to the semi-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The following year, after helping his nation finish third at the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Nations_League" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 UEFA Nations League">UEFA Nations League</a> and qualify for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a>, Henderson was named <a href="/wiki/The_FA_England_Awards#Senior_Men&#39;s_Player_of_the_Year" title="The FA England Awards">England Player of the Year</a>, in the process becoming the first player to win the award at both U21 and senior level.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Henderson_20141221_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jordan_Henderson_20141221_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Jordan_Henderson_20141221_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jordan_Henderson_20141221_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Jordan_Henderson_20141221_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jordan_Henderson_20141221_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Jordan_Henderson_20141221_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1505" data-file-height="2321" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Henderson_20141221_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henderson playing for Liverpool in 2014</div></div></div>
<p>Henderson usually plays as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Box-to-box_midfielder" title="Midfielder">box-to-box midfielder</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> although under Klopp he has mostly been used as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Defensive_midfielder" title="Midfielder">defensive midfielder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> However, with the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Fabinho_(footballer,_born_1993)" title="Fabinho (footballer, born 1993)">Fabinho</a> in 2018, Henderson moved back to his original "number 8" position as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Central_midfielder" title="Midfielder">central midfielder</a> closer to the right side of the pitch, a role in which he excels the most.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reinvention_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reinvention-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> A versatile player,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> he has also been used in a more <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">advanced midfield</a> role on occasion,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and even as a makeshift <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)#Centre-back" title="Defender (association football)">centre-back</a> during periods of injury crisis among Liverpool's central defenders.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> He is widely regarded as a player who works hard and brings energy to the team.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Described as an "athletic and hardworking midfielder," Henderson has developed his game during his time at Liverpool, evolving into a more complete player; in particular, former Liverpool player <a href="/wiki/Danny_Murphy_(footballer,_born_1977)" title="Danny Murphy (footballer, born 1977)">Danny Murphy</a> noted in 2020 that his passing range had increased, which allowed him to take on an increasingly more creative role for his team.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, he constantly presses high up the field whenever the opposition is in possession.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Besides physical attributes and footballing skills, he has also been praised for his tactical intelligence,<sup id="cite_ref-evolved_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evolved-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> consistency,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> and his leadership, both on and outside the pitch.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> He is also known for his ability to win challenges, transition the ball forward, and make attacking runs from midfield to get into good offensive positions.<sup id="cite_ref-reinvention_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reinvention-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Although he drew criticism in the media in his earlier career for being a dispensable player, he later drew praise from pundits for his ability to develop his game and establish himself as an important midfielder in his team, with <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo">Flamengo</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Jesus" title="Jorge Jesus">Jorge Jesus</a> describing him as "best midfielder in the world in his position," in 2020, following their encounter in the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2019 FIFA Club World Cup Final">2019 FIFA Club World Cup Final</a>, while his Liverpool coach Klopp instead described him as "exceptional" and "outstanding."<sup id="cite_ref-reinvention_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reinvention-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-evolved_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evolved-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, Steven Gerrard said about Henderson, "Teams can't function at Liverpool's level without a cog like Jordan Henderson."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Henderson studied at <a href="/wiki/Farringdon_Community_Sports_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Farringdon Community Sports College">Farringdon Community Sports College</a> before joining Sunderland as a youngster.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> He is a Sunderland fan and attended the <a href="/wiki/2014_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2014 Football League Cup Final">2014 League Cup Final</a> with the Sunderland fans, while being a player at Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> On the same day as being named Liverpool captain, it was announced he would also be featuring alongside <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a> on the cover of the UK edition of <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_16" title="FIFA 16">FIFA 16</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Henderson and his wife Rebecca Burnett have three children.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> His father Brian, a former policeman and amateur footballer, survived <a href="/wiki/Oral_cancer" title="Oral cancer">oral cancer</a> during Henderson's early Liverpool career and was able to attend the 2019 Champions League final in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom">COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom</a>, Henderson, as captain of Liverpool, contacted fellow Premier League captains to organise a coronavirus fund that would raise millions of pounds for the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">NHS</a>. His idea was for Premier League footballers to contribute to a fund for frontline NHS workers.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Henderson earned praise for his allyship in the wake of the annual Premier League Rainbow Laces campaign for his supportive words for a young LGBT fan. <sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jordan_Henderson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
